        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158450297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5182346581288618223"><i> Every 7 years, Ordeen will come to Greece and makes a bloodbath everytime she comes.<br/>But not now, because Mam doesn't intended to let her back. Especially when the Fiend is unleashed.<br/>And to prevent Ordeen, Mam needs allies. Either from the Light, or the Dark. </i><br/><br/><br/>one of my favorite series, nowadays. So the review!<br/><br/><br/><u> The characters </u><br/>they're changed throughout this series. Either they're better, or worse.<br/>I like to see how they'll end up like.<br/><br/>Tom seems to be much more impulsive than he's ever been. He isn</span>
  <span id="freeText5182346581288618223" style="display:none"><i> Every 7 years, Ordeen will come to Greece and makes a bloodbath everytime she comes.<br />But not now, because Mam doesn't intended to let her back. Especially when the Fiend is unleashed.<br />And to prevent Ordeen, Mam needs allies. Either from the Light, or the Dark. </i><br /><br /><br />one of my favorite series, nowadays. So the review!<br /><br /><br /><u> The characters </u><br />they're changed throughout this series. Either they're better, or worse.<br />I like to see how they'll end up like.<br /><br />Tom seems to be much more impulsive than he's ever been. He isn't whiny, but he's just being too pessimistic it almost makes me want to shout. I mean, yeah, everything is at stake, but if he's being more optimist, he can see everything more clearly and maybe see opportunities.<br /><br />While Alice, I thought she's taking herself as being daughter to the Fiend too bad. It scares her too much and makes her desperately does anything to save Tom.<br />Plus, she's weaker in this book, not as brave in earlier books.<br />She's more girly-like...<br /><br />Spook. I really want to get the hell out of him somehow. He even isn't as useful as his apprentice!<br /><br />Bill Arkwright. He's childish, not a good teacher but much nicer Spook. Still, I can understand why Spook treats him like he's still his apprentice...<br /><br />Mam. What to say about her? She makes me remember one thing, <i> 'the enemy of your enemy, is your ally'. </i><br /><br />Mab. I didn't know, why is she so... What-do-you-call-it with Tom? Is she's going to be Alice's rival in love? If so, it'll be failed love triangle.<br /><br />Grimalkin. Should I say that she's so cool?<br />I think everyone knows that already.<br /><br /><br /><u> The story </u> it's a little hard to process somehow, maybe my being for too close with exam time made my imagination a little too hard to reach.<br /><br />Well, I hated the Spook's pride, I knew about sticking with principles, but he judges too... Well, I hated it.<br /><br />Plus, Tom always thinks about loyalty, and it sucks. Why can't he be more rebel or what? But I can hardly think Tom as a rebel, it just doesn't match his character.<br />Even though well, I thanked him for saving Alice, she's one of my favorite.<br /><br />And yeah, I could feel romance in the air. Or that Tom's protectiveness over Alice. Or Mab's getting her way between them. Or The Spook's way to separate them (no matter what Mam says).<br />Just, whatever.<br /><br /><br />Still, this series is a looong way to go and I think, somehow it almost just like copying the earlier books.<br />Hope it won't last long, or I'll get bored.<br /><br /><br />PS. I could make a full review without spoiler bleeding in every word!</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_63323610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63323610" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2440086-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546536963p2/2440086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63323610?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/2440086-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061344626" href="/book/show/6240917-clash-of-the-demons">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2440086-becky?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2440086-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63323610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3745480228943499528">I'm a long-time fan of the adventures of Thomas Ward, the Spook's apprentice. His story started with Revenge of the Witch and now Clash of the Demons is the sixth book in this genuinely frightening series. The story is told from Tom's perspective in the first person so the reader is completely inside his head. Delaney pulls you into Tom's world and makes you feel for him and care about everyone he loves.<br/><br/>For those who need a little Last Apprentice tutorial, Tom Ward is the seventh son of a sevent</span>
  <span id="freeText3745480228943499528" style="display:none">I'm a long-time fan of the adventures of Thomas Ward, the Spook's apprentice. His story started with Revenge of the Witch and now Clash of the Demons is the sixth book in this genuinely frightening series. The story is told from Tom's perspective in the first person so the reader is completely inside his head. Delaney pulls you into Tom's world and makes you feel for him and care about everyone he loves.<br /><br />For those who need a little Last Apprentice tutorial, Tom Ward is the seventh son of a seventh son. This means that he can see and do things that normal people cannot. In the first book he is apprenticed to John Gregory, the county Spook. A Spook's job is to protect the county from evil; witches, boggarts, etc. Tom is John Gregory's last apprentice and his most powerful. Their adventures take them all over the county to face various evil creatures, including the Fiend/Devil himself!<br /><br />In this installment in the series we finally get to learn more about Tom's Mam. She's always been an enigmatic, endearing character, but now Delaney lets the reader in on her back story. Tom travels with his master, John Gregory, his friend, Alice and another Spook, Bill Arkwright to Greece to help his Mam face a powerful servant of the dark. The relationships between these five characters are so dynamic and interesting that they will draw the reader in as much as the action...and there is plenty of action.<br /><br />I'm not an easy scare when it comes to books (movies are a different story!), but this series has always given me the creeps and this sixth title does not disappoint. Delaney never really goes for the full on gross out fear, but instead scares the reader with a slow build. The evil characters are really evil, but even those characters who fight for the light are starting to fall into shades of gray. Tom faces some of the scariest evil yet while he battles with his own inner conflict of dark vs. light. This book will have young readers rushing to turn on all the lights in the house and even adults will want to plug in a nightlight...just in case.<br /><br />If you don't read this series, you should stop reading this and run out to the bookstore/library to pick up a copy of Revenge of the Witch and if you already are a Tom Ward fan then reserve your copy of Clash of the Demons now! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3745480228943499528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_759923344" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759923344" />
    <a title="Audiobooks_Rock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3464317-audiobooks-rock"><img alt="Audiobooks_Rock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432038015p2/3464317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/759923344?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Audiobooks_Rock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Audiobooks_Rock" href="/user/show/3464317-audiobooks-rock">Audiobooks_Rock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759923344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13572833093666411244">So why have I given this book such a tough rating?<br/>The answer is simple. from this book and onwards, the world Mr Delaney build gets ripped to shreds. The story becomes one of herculian proportions and irish legends. This book is in my opinion the moment this series broke. <br/><br/>I really liked the first 4 books, the 5th was pretty good too, but from there on its all 1 big mish mash of legends and stories that ruin the original story for me. I did not want to read an epic story. But that is what the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText13572833093666411244" style="display:none">So why have I given this book such a tough rating?<br />The answer is simple. from this book and onwards, the world Mr Delaney build gets ripped to shreds. The story becomes one of herculian proportions and irish legends. This book is in my opinion the moment this series broke. <br /><br />I really liked the first 4 books, the 5th was pretty good too, but from there on its all 1 big mish mash of legends and stories that ruin the original story for me. I did not want to read an epic story. But that is what the book series now turns into: an epic mythology story.<br /><br />At first the county could have been anywhere in an other world. But from this book onwards suddenly its somewhere in Britain. since Greece, Scotland and Ireland come into play. its like Mr Delaney decided one morning that he did not want to write this series anymore, but wanted to write greek and irish legends. why call the county the county, when u suddenly decide its somewhere in england?<br /><br />I feel like the story was destroyed by its own authors lack of imagination for countries. and by the fact that he wanted to write something completely different half way. After this book, and the next 3. I decided it was better to drop the series, and decide that book 4 was the end of it. Reading further, is absolutely not worth it. whilst book 5 is still true to the series and fun, book 4ths ending is the best you can get.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13572833093666411244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J5/HRdnKMfscVMVXqfB6lIlsh2y4N+rTXxFypayMUmQe7y+LtgJ452dbjU1WpWPlayUTm4act0rrtOsseVWh7A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('abHlYyeAwDOf/0n26N+t5EN52LfhnE2lgmBtKxZDh1pQwQ2tSEiJL+TwAewXirSVoTBMQN83EDw2xfSiw5p00g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney">About Joseph Delaney</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1376358484p3/146374.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/146374.Joseph_Delaney">Joseph Delaney
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8456392729773426851">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br/>He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br/><br/>He first got the idea for the Spooks series when </span>
  <span id="freeText8456392729773426851" style="display:none">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br />He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br /><br />He first got the idea for the Spooks series when he moved to the village where he lives now and discovered there was a local boggart - ‘a man like me needs boggarts around’. He made a note in his notebook ‘a story about a man who hunts boggarts’ and years later when he had to come up with an idea at short notice developed this into ‘The Spook’s Apprentice’, the first book in the series.<br />He continues to draw upon the folklore of Lancashire and has acquired much local knowledge over the years which he tweaks and modifies to create his fictional world. Another source of inspiration has been Lancashire's varied and atmospheric landscape. Many of the locations in the County are based on actual places in Lancashire. <br />In the early days of his writing career Joseph worked as a teacher at a Sixth Form College: his subjects were English, Film and Media Studies. He used to get up early and write every morning before work. That way he could write a book a year – which promptly got rejected! When the Americans bought the series he decided to give up teaching and write full time. <br />Prior to teaching he worked as an engineer in his twenties, completing an apprenticeship just like Tom Ward in the spook’s books.<br />Joseph describes his method of writing as a process of discovery. He doesn’t plot too far ahead and often doesn’t know what is going to happen until he writes it down. In other words he makes it up as he goes along. He prefers writing dialogue to description, in which he says he is a minimalist and leaves much to the reader’s imagination. <br />Joseph has three children and nine grandchildren and is a wonderful public speaker available for conference, library and bookshop events.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426629.The_Spook_s_Curse" title="The Spook's Curse" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Curse</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426189.The_Spook_s_Secret" title="The Spook's Secret" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Secret</a> have all been shortlisted for the Lancashire children's Book for the Year Award. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a> is the winner of both the Sefton Book Award and the Hampshire Book Award.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.josephdelaneyauthor.com">www.josephdelaneyauthor.com</a><br /><br /><br /><i>from <a href="http://www.rbooks.co.uk/author.aspx?id=15205" rel="nofollow noopener">publisher's website</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8456392729773426851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
